Jamison Brereton

10 (836)
Dialogue of Yama and Yam─▒╠Д
Yama Vaivasvata and Yam─л Vaivasvat─л
14 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh
This justly famous (and much discussed) hymn presents a tense dialogue between a pair of twins, the male Yama and female Yam─л (yama╠Б means тАЬtwinтАЭ; yam─л╠Б is the feminine form), who become the first mortals. Yam─л╠Б, who speaks first, urges her twin brother to have sex with her, so that they can have children and continue their line in the approved manner. Yama indignantly rejects her advances, outraged by the idea of incest and certain that the divine guardians of moral order will see the act and punish them.
It is impossible in a short introduction to do justice to the richness of this hymn and the extraordinary skill with which the poet deploys grammatical categories such as person, number, and verb modality in service of the condensed drama of their encounter. Both Yam─л and Yama make legalistic arguments, often using juridi
cal turns of phrase, and especially in the first part of the hymn they distance the personal and emotional implications of their speech by regularly using plural and 3rd-person forms to refer to each other. It is not until the last word of verse 4 that one of them uses a 1st-person dual (тАЬwe twoтАЭ) form. They also use dueling divine models for the relationships they are arguing for: Yama cites their near ancestors, тАЬthe Gandharva in the waters and the watery maiden,тАЭ as reason not to violate the incest taboo (vs. 4) and Mitra and Varuс╣Зa as stern enforcers (vs. 6) with spies everywhere (vs. 8)тАФwhile Yam─л claims that Tvaс╣гс╣нar, who shapes embryos in the womb, made them a married couple already in the womb (vs. 5) and twice (vss. 5, 9) invokes as their divine counterparts Heaven and Earth, a notoriously incestuous pair (as she makes quite explicit in 9c). The use and placement of kinship terms

in the hymn is also notable, including the fact that тАЬbrotherтАЭ and тАЬsisterтАЭ are not encountered until verse 11. It is also striking that the names of the speakers do not appear until verse 7.
The emotional temperature of the hymn rises significantly at that very point. Yam─л abandons her legalistic argumentsтАФthat they need to have offspring, that they were already a married couple in the wombтАФin favor of a naked expression of sexual desire. Yama remains unmoved, but the roiling emotions are reflected in the ragged meter of some of the later verses (12тАУ13), especially in the latter verse where Yam─л breaks off her speech in frustration in a very short p─Бda containing two occurrences of a word (bata╠Б) found nowhere else and exhibiting aberrant phonology. Our render
ing of the word aims at the level of slangy insult to which bata╠Б appears to belong. The hymn ends in an impasse. Yama remains obdurate and urges Yam─л to find another loverтАФa difficult quest when there are no other mortals! However, given the rest of his history, sketched briefly above, we must assume that he gave in in the end, on the evidence of X.13.4.

010-019 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton

The next ten hymns (X.10тАУ19) form a Yama cycle, though the subject matter found in the individual hymns is quite various. Yama, the son of Vivasvant, is king of the land of the dead because he was the first mortal to die. Yet he was apparently born immortal (see esp. I.83.5) and chose to become mortal, subject to death, тАЬfor the sake of the gods…and for the sake of offspringтАЭ (X.13.4). The opening hymn in the cycle, the dialogue of Yama and his twin sister Yam─л, on the fraught topic of embarking on incestuous sex in order to produce offspring, addresses YamaтАЩs change of status and his choice, but in a deliberately oblique and misleading fashion, as Yama spurns the sexual advances of his sister, and at the end of their bitter argument there seems little likelihood of children. The last six hymns in this cycle (X.14тАУ19) are collectively known as funeral hymns. The first, X.14, is devoted especially to Yama in his role as king of the realm of the dead, while the others, especially 15тАУ18, concern various aspects of death and the treatment of the deadтАФfor example, the forefathers who preceded us to YamaтАЩs realm in X.15, the cremation fire in X.16, the funeral itself in X.

The intermediate hymns, X.11тАУ13, have less superficially clear connections to the Yama saga, but both X.12 (vss. 6тАУ7) and X.13 (vss. 4тАУ5) make important comments on Yama and on YamaтАЩs choice.

There is also an underlying unifying theme, that of duality and twinned-ness: the absolute disjunction between and the ultimate complementarity and unity of the mortal and the immortal, life and death, men and gods, men and women, heaven and earth, sacred and profane. It is appropriate that the cycle should begin with the dialogue between the primal twins, Yama and Yam─л, whose very names mean тАЬtwinтАЭ and who bridge the gap between mortal and immortal.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Yami speaks). The immortals take plural asure in (a union) like this which is forbidden to every mortal; letyour mind then concur with mine, and as the progenitor (of all) was the husband (of his daughter), do you enjoymy person n.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Which is forbidden: tyajasam = that which is to be left or avoided, illicit, such as the intercourse ofbrahm─Б with his daughter;

Ekasya = Praj─Бpati, as chief of the whole world;

Tyajasam = that which is abandonedor given to another, viz., women, daughters etc. The word may also mean descendants, lit. those who are left,scions, offshoots, and so, the reading may be: this is what the gods themselves desire offspring from one aloneof mankind

Jamison Brereton

[Yam─л:] The immortals do want this: a legacy of the one and only mortal. Your mind has (already) been set upon my mind, upon me. As husband, you should enter the body of (your) wife.

Griffith

Yea, this the Immortals seek of thee with longing, progeny of the sole existing mortal.
Then let thy soul and mine be knit together, and as a loving husband take thy consort.

Geldner

Die Unsterblichen wollen gerade das: einen Leibeserben von dem einzigen Sterblichen. Dein Sinn soll sich unserem Sinne f├╝gen; als Gatte sollst du in deines Weibes Leib eingehen!

Grassmann

┬╗Die G├╢tter eben sind’s, die dieses wollen, vom einzigen der Menschen einen Spr├╢ssling; Es ist uns eng geschlossen Seel’ an Seele, so geh als Gatte in der Gattin Leib ein.┬л

English translation:

тАЬ(Yama speak). We have not done what was done formerly; for how can we who speak truth, utter nowthat which is untrue? Gandharva (the sun) was in the watery (firmament), and the water was his bride. She is ourcommon hence our near affinity.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Yama:] What we have not done before, should (we do it) now? While proclaiming truths, we would [/should we] murmur untruth?
The Gandharva in the waters and the watery maidenтАФthat is our
umbilical tie; therefore our kinship is of the highest.

Griffith

Shall we do now what we ne’er did aforetime? we who spake righteously now talk impurely?
Gandharva in the floods, the Dame of Waters-such is our bond, such our most lofty kinship.

Geldner

Was wir fr├╝her nicht getan haben, sollen wir das jetzt tun? Das Rechte redend w├╝rden wir Unrechtes fl├╝stern. Gandharva in dem Wasser und die Wasserfrau, die sind unser Ursprung, das ist unsere h├╢chste Blutsverwandtschaft.

Grassmann

Wie? sollen jetzt wir thun, was nie wir thaten, das Rechte redend doch dem Unrecht fr├╢hnen? Gandharva in dem Luftmeer und die Meerfrau sind Aeltern uns, und wir die N├дchstverwandten.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Yami speaks). The divine omniform genitive rator Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б, the progenitor, made us two husband andwife, even in the womb: none frustrate his undertaking; earth and heaven are conscious of this our (union).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Yam─л:] (Even) in the womb the Begetter made us two a married couple, god Tvaс╣гс╣нar, the impeller who provides all forms.
No one transgresses his commandments. Heaven and Earth take heed of this about us.

Griffith

Even in the womb God Tvastar, Vivifier, shaping all forms, Creator, made us consorts.
None violates his holy ordinances: that we are his the heavens and earth acknowledge.

Geldner

Schon im Mutterleib hat uns der Sch├╢pfer zu Ehegatten gemacht, der Gott Tvastri, der Bestimmer, der alle Formen bildet. Nicht ├╝bertreten sie seine Gebote; dessen sind uns Erde und Himmel Zeugen.

Grassmann

┬╗Im Mutterleib schon zeugte uns zu Gatten Gott Tvaschtar, der gestaltenreiche Bildner, Und dessen Ordnung darf man nicht verletzen, dess sind uns Zeugen Himmel auch und Erde.┬л

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(Yama speaks). Who knows anything of this (his) first day (of existence)? Who has beheld it? Whohas here revealed it? The dwelling of Mitra and of Varuс╣Зa is vast. What say you, who punishes men with hell?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dwelling of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa: the revolution of day and night; what say…hell: what say you, wanton one, falselyabout men? Who punishes: ahanaс╕е is a male; therefore, Yam─л is made the speaker of the last part of the verse

Jamison Brereton

[Yama:] Who knows about this first day? Who has seen it; who will proclaim it here?
Lofty is the ordinance of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa. Will you speak about
superior men [=gods] with deviant (speech), lubricious one?

English translation:

тАЬ(Yami speaks). The desire of Yama has approached me Yam─л, to lie with him in the same bed; I willabandon my person n as a wife to her husband; let us exert ourselves in union like the two wheels of a wagon.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Yam─л:] Desire for Yama has come to me, Yam─л, to lie together in the same womb [/place].
Like a wife to her husband I would yield my body. We would тАЬlet тАЩer ripтАЭ like two chariot wheels.

Griffith

I, Yami, am possessed by love of Yama, that I may rest on the same couch beside him.
I as a wife would yield me to my husband. Like car-wheels let us speed to meet each other.

рдпрдореНрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдЦреНрдпрд╛рддреЛ рдпрдордГ рдкреБрдирд░рд╛рд╣ ред рдЗрд╣ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рд▓реНрдБрд▓реЛрдХреЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рдирдГ рдпреЗ рд╕реНрдкрд╢рдГ рдЕрд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рджрдпрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд░рд╛рдГ рдЪрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рд╢реБрднрд╛рд╢реБрднрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдХрд░реНрдордкреНрд░рддреНрдпрд╡реЗрдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдкрд░рд┐рднреНрд░рдордиреНрддрд┐ рдПрддреЗ рдЪрд╛рд░рд╛рдГ рдХреНрд╖рдгрдорд╛рддреНрд░рдордкрд┐ рдЪрд░рдгрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рд░рд░рд╣рд┐рддрд╛рдГ рди рддрд┐рд╖реНрдардиреНрддрд┐ ред рди рдирд┐ рдорд┐рд╖рдиреНрддрд┐ рдореЗрд╖рдгрдВ рди рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд╢реБрднрдорд╢реБрднрдВ рд╡рд╛ рдпрдГ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ рддрдВ рдирд┐рд░реАрдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддреЗ рдЪреЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╣реЗ рдЖрд╣рдирдГ рдордорд╛рдкрд╣рдиреНрддреНрд░рд┐ рдЕрд╕рд╣реНрдпрднрд╛рд╖рдгреЗрди рджреБрдГрдЦрдпрд┐рддреНрд░рд┐ рддреНрд╡рдВ рдорддреН рдорддреНрддрдГ рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрди рддреНрд╡рддреНрд╕рджреГрд╢реЗрди рд╕рд╣ рддреВрдпрдВ рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрд░рдВ рдпрд╛рд╣рд┐ рд╕рдВрдЧрдЪреНрдЫ ред рдЧрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЪ рддреЗрди рд╡рд┐ рд╡реГрд╣ рдзрд░реНрдорд╛рд░реНрдердХрд╛рдорд╛рдиреБрджреНрдпрдЪреНрдЫ ред рддрддреНрд░ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ ред рд░рдереНрдпреЗрд╡ рдЪрдХреНрд░рд╛ ред рдпрдерд╛ рд░рдерд╛рд╡рдпрд╡рднреВрддреЗ рдЪрдХреНрд░реЗ рд░рдердореБрджреНрдпрдЪреНрдЫрддрд╕реНрддрджреНрд╡рддреН рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Yama speaks). The spies of the gods, which wander upon earth, never stop, never close their eyeс╣гAssociate quickly, destructress, with some other than with me, and exert yourselves in union, like the two wheelsof a wagon.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Destructress: i.e., causing unhappiness by your shameful conversation

Jamison Brereton

[Yama:] They do not stand still; they do not blinkтАФthe spies of the gods who roam about here.
With another than me, lubricious one, drive off straightaway; with him тАЬlet тАЩer ripтАЭ like two chariot wheels.

Griffith

They stand not still, they never close their eyelids, those sentinels of Gods who wander round us.
Not me-go quickly, wanton, with another, and hasten like a chariot wheel to meet him.

(рдЖрд╣рдирдГ) рд╣реЗ рд╣реГрджрдпрдкреАрдбрд┐рдХреЗ ! рдпрд╣ рддреЛ рдЕрд╕рд╛рдзреНрдп рджреБрдГрдЦ рд╣реИ, рдЗрд╕рд▓рд┐рдпреЗ (рдорддреН) рдореБрдЭ рд╕реЗ рднрд┐рдиреНрди (рдЕрдиреНрдпреЗрди) рдЬреЛ рдХреЛрдИ рдЕрдиреНрдп рдкреБрд░реБрд╖ рддреБрдЭреЗ рджрд┐рдЦрд▓рд╛рдИ рдкреЬреЗ, рдЙрд╕рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рддреВрдпрдореН)рд╢реАрдШреНрд░(рдпрд╛рд╣рд┐) рддреВ рд╕рдорд╛рдЧрдо рдХреЛрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛ (рддреЗрди) рдЙрд╕реА рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде (рд╡рд┐рд╡реГрд╣) рдЧрд╛рд░реНрд╣рд╕реНрдереНрдпрднрд╛рд░ рдХреЛ рдЙрдард╛ рдФрд░ (рд░рдереНрдпреЗрд╡ рдЪрдХреНрд░рд╛) рд░рде рдХреЗ рдкрд╣рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рд╕рдорд╛рди рд╡рд╣рди рдХрд░ реереорее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╣рднрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░рдпреЛрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ рдпрдорд╛рдп рдХрд▓реНрдкрд┐рддрдВ рднрд╛рдЧрдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирдГ рджрд╢рд╕реНрдпреЗрддреН рдкреНрд░рдпрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ ред рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐ рдЪрдХреНрд╖реБрдГ рддреЗрдЬрдГ рдореБрд╣реБрдГ рдореБрд╣реБрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ рдпрдорд╛рдп рдЙрдиреНрдорд┐рдореАрдпрд╛рддреН рдЙрджреЗрддреБред рджрд┐рд╡рд╛ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛ рджреНрдпрд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реАрднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╕рд╣ рдорд┐рдереБрдирд╛ рдорд┐рдереБрдиреМ рд╕рдмрдиреНрдзреВ рд╕рдорд╛рдирдмрдиреНрдзреВ рдЕрд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдореИ рдпрдорд╛рдп ред рдПрддрдЬреНрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЗрдпрдВ рдпрдореАрдГ рдпрдорд╕реНрдп рдЕрдЬрд╛рдорд┐ рдЕрднреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдВ рдмрд┐рднреГрдпрд╛рддреН рдзрд╛рд░рдпрддреБ ред рдпрд╛рдиреЗрди рдкрд░рд┐рдЧреГрд╣реНрдгрд╛рддреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Yami speaks). To him (Yam) let every worshipper sacrifice both day and night, on him let the eye ofthe Sun repeatedly rise; (for him may) the kindred pair (day and night unite) with heaven and earth. Yama willadhere to the non- affinity of Yama.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yama will adhere: or, may Yam─л bear patiently Yama’s unbrotherly (refusal)

Jamison Brereton

[Yam─л:] Night and day she would do service to him. She could for an instant trip up the eye of the sun.
The couple has the same (kin-)ties as Heaven and Earth. Yam─л could bear the unbrotherly (act) of Yama.

Griffith

May Surya’s eye with days and nights endow him, and ever may his light spread out before him.
In heaven and earth the kindred Pair commingle. On Yam! be the unbrotherly act of Yama.

Geldner

Sie w├╝rde ihm Tag und Nacht gef├дllig sein, sie w├╝rde f├╝r ein Weilchen das Auge der Sonne t├дuschen. Mit Himmel und Erde steht das Paar in gleichem Verwandtschaftsverh├дltnis. Yami w├╝rde des Yama ungeschwisterliches Tun auf sich nehmen.

Grassmann

┬╗Sie will bei Tag und Nacht ihm gern bereit stehn, der Sonne Auge m├╢g’ ein Weilchen schlummern, Gleich Erd’ und Himmel paaren sich Geschwister; gern will des Jama Blutschuld Jam─л tragen.┬л

Elizarenkova

рдпрддреНрд░ рдпреЗрд╖реБ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗрд╖реБ рдЬрд╛рдордпрдГ рднрдЧрд┐рдиреНрдпрдГ рдЕрдЬрд╛рдорд┐ рдЕрднреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдВ рдкрддрд┐рдВ рдХреГрдгрд╡рдиреН рдХрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрд╛ рддрд╛рдирд┐ рдЙрддреНрддрд░рд╛ рдЙрддреНрддрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ рдпреБрдЧрд╛рдирд┐ рдХрд╛рд▓рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рдГ рдЖ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрд╛рдиреН рдЖрдЧрдорд┐рд╖реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ред рдШ рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреВрд░рдгрдГ ред рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреЗрд╡рдВ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреНрдзреЗ рд╕реБрднрдЧреЗ рддреНрд╡рдорд┐рджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рдорддреН рдорддреНрддрдГ рдЕрдиреНрдпрдВ рдкрддрд┐рдВ рднрд░реНрддрд╛рд░рдореН рдЗрдЪреНрдЫрд╕реНрд╡ рдХрд╛рдордпрд╕реНрд╡ ред рддрджрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╡реГрд╖рднрд╛рдп рддрд╡ рдпреЛрдиреМ рд░реЗрддрдГ рд╕реЗрдХреНрддреНрд░реЗ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рдп рдЖрддреНрдореАрдпрдВ рдмрд╛рд╣реБрдореН рдЙрдк рдмрд░реНрдмреГрд╣рд┐ред рд╢рдпрдирдХрд╛рд▓ рдЙрдкрдмрд░реНрд╣рдгрдВ рдХреБрд░реБ рее рее рен рее

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН

There will come future yuga-s when siblings will perform unkindredly acts.

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН - рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

A prophesy of the downward yuga-s in the RV?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Yama speaks). The subsequent ages will come, when sisters will choose one who is not a brother (asa husband); therefore, auspicious one, choose another husband than me, and make your arm a pillow for yourmate.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Yama:] Later generations will come, in which kin will perform the unkindred (act).
Keep plumping up your arm as pillow for a (real) bull. Seek another than me as husband, well-portioned one.

Griffith

Sure there will come succeeding times when brothers and sisters will do acts unmeet for kinsfolk.
Not me, O fair one,-seek another husband, and make thine arm a pillow for thy consort.

Geldner

Es werden sp├дter solche Geschlechter kommen, wo Geschwister Ungeschwisterliches treiben. Leg einem Bullen deinen Arm unter, such dir einen anderen als mich zum Gatten, Holde!

Grassmann

Wohl m├╢gen kommen sp├дtere Geschlechter, wo Blutsverwandte Blutschuld auf sich laden, So schlinge fest den Arm um einen Gatten, w├дhl’ einen andern dir, als mich, o Sch├╢ne.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(Yami speaks). Is he a brother whose sister has no lord? Is she a sister (whose brother) misfortuneapproaches? Overcome by desire, I strongly urge this one request; unite your person n with mine.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Misfortune:decay; Nirс╣Ыti is a person nification. The meaning is, a true brother will not let his sister lack a husband, and a truesister will not let her brother lack a wife

Jamison Brereton

[Yam─л:] What will тАЬbrotherтАЭ (mean) when there will be no refuge. And what will тАЬsister,тАЭ if Dissolution will come down?
Driven by desire many times I murmur this: mingle your body with
my body.

Griffith

Is he a brother when no lord is left her? Is she a sister when Destruction cometh?
Forced by my love these many words I utter. Come near, and hold me in thy close embraces.

Geldner

Was soll dann der Bruder, wenn man schutzlos sein soll? Was die Schwester, wenn das Verderben hereinbrechen soll? Von Liebe toll fl├╝stere ich das immer wieder: Vereine deinen Leib mit dem meinen!

Grassmann

┬╗Was ist der Bruder, wenn er ohne Schutz l├дsst, und was die Schwester, wenn ihr naht Verderben, Von Lieb’ ergriffen fleh’ ich stets dies eine, lass deinen Leib mit meinem sich vermischen.┬л

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(Yama speaks). I will not unite my person n with yours; they call him who approaches a sister, a sinneс╣ЫEnjoy plural asure with some other than me; your brother, auspicious one, has no such desire.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

[Yama:] Verily, I must not mingle my body with your body. They call him evil who will go down on his sister.
With another than me arrange your pleasures. Your brother does not want this, well-portioned one.

Griffith

I will not fold mine arms about thy body: they call it sin when one comes near his sister.
Not me,-prepare thy pleasures with another: thy brother seeks not this from thee, O fair one.

English translation:

тАЬ(Yami speaks). Alas, Yama, you are feeble; we understand not your mind or your heart. Some otherfemale embraces you as a girth a horse, or as a creeper a tree.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Alas! bato bat─Бsi = you are feeble, feeble; thepada text is: bata asi;

Bata = pitiable, anukampya┼Ыc─Бsi, or, alas!

Jamison Brereton

[Yam─л:] You jerk, you really are a jerk, Yama! Truly we have not found mind and heart in you.
Another (woman) will surely embrace you, like a girthband a yoked
(horse), like a vine a tree.

Griffith

Alas! thou art indeed a weakling, Yama we find in thee no trace of heart or spirit.
As round the tree the woodbine clings, another will cling albout thee girt as with a girdle.

Geldner

O Elend, ein Elender bist du, Yama! Mitnichten haben wir Sinn und Herz von dir gewonnen. Eine andere wird dich gewi├Я umschlingen wie der Gurt das geschirrte Ro├Я, wie die Rankepflanze den Baum.

Grassmann

┬╗Ein Stein f├╝rwahr bist Jama du, und niemals hab ich dein Herz und deinen Sinn gewonnen, Ein andres Weib wird wie das Ross der Leibgurt und wie den Baum die Ranke dich umschlingen.┬л

Elizarenkova
